## codex: 1. Fix the 4 broken imports in executor.py's real ...

1. Fix the 4 broken imports in executor.py's real backend.
  find_path → pathfind, result["path"] → result["route"], add serial param to tap/swipe, 
  observe → build_observations. 30 minutes. Without this, zero tooling works live.       

  2. Wire PilotBridge as an executor backend option.
  adb_bridge.screencap returns blank on MEmu. PilotBridge (DroidCast) is the only working
   screenshot path. The executor needs a pilot_backend() alongside default_backend() and 
  mock_backend().

  3. Add page_hq to graph.json and fix the nav paths.
  The agent proved HQ is a real screen between main and dorm/cat-lodge/academy. The graph
   skips it. Also fix tasks.json referencing page_dormevent which doesn't exist in the   
  graph.

  4. Add arrival verification to _navigate_real().
  After executing taps, call locate() to confirm we actually arrived. Right now it       
  blindly returns success. This is the difference between "navigation" and "hoping."     

  5. Build a locate_validate CLI mode for the exploring agent.
  python scripts/locate.py --screenshot data/screenshots/wf_dorm_main.png --graph        
  graph.json — returns what state it thinks we're in. The agent runs this after every    
  screenshot during exploration. Tells us instantly which anchors work and which are     
  garbage.

  6. Build scripts/emulator_startup.py.
  The ensure_game_ready() state machine: find emulator window → start if needed → ADB    
  connect → ATX init → launch game → wait through black screen → tap title → dismiss     
  popups → confirm page_main. System-level screenshots, not ADB, for the waiting phase.  

  7. Build scripts/daemon.py.
  The glue: pick_next() → execute_task() → compute_next_run() → sleep → repeat. With     
  error_strategy enforcement, circuit breaker (3 failures → disable), re-locate on       
  startup, and SIGINT handling.

  8. Wire execution_event_log.py into executor and daemon.
  Every task start, state change, tap, navigation, error, and escalation writes to       
  NDJSON. Without this we're flying blind during automated runs.

  9. Extract load_json() to scripts/utils.py.
  It's in 10 files. Quick cleanup that prevents the next person from adding an 11th copy.

  10. Add integration tests: scheduler→executor round-trip + default_backend import test.
  One test that loads tasks.json, picks a task, executes it through the mock, and        
  verifies the full loop. One test that instantiates default_backend() (and
  pilot_backend()) to catch import crashes — so we never ship broken wiring again.

## codex: What do you think of this criticism? oc refactor o...

What do you think of this criticism? oc refactor opinion:

The current CLAUDE.md and AGENTS.md on this branch are already well-positioned. Here's what I'd prioritize next:

Add automation-runtime-consolidation.md to AGENTS.md's required reading table — it's now committed but not in the index. New agents won't find it. One-liner addition.

Create docs/runtime-api-spec.md — CLAUDE.md and AGENTS.md both describe the three-tier interface (where_am_i(), navigate_to(), execute_task(), ensure_game_ready()) but there's no canonical spec doc. The plans doc has items 11-12 calling for runtime_api.py; the spec should precede the implementation so the interface is pinned before it's built.

Extract the ALAS operational block from CLAUDE.md — the "Optional ALAS observation workflow" section with the PowerShell launch/venv scripts is correct (it IS optional), but it's taking up 40+ lines in the prime orientation doc. Move it to docs/alas-setup.md and replace with a one-line pointer. CLAUDE.md should be about SC conventions, not ALAS management.

plan.md is safe as-is — I searched and it doesn't reference the old "ALAS harness = live runtime" framing. NORTH_STAR.md already mentions the "Agent Control Surface" concept accurately. No urgent corrections needed there.

What doesn't need doing: the ALAS-to-SC mapping table in AGENTS.md is great and should stay. The three-tier API description at the top of both CLAUDE.md and AGENTS.md is the right anchor for new agent sessions.

## codex: Response to Agent

Response to Agent
Answers to Your Questions
What does "maximum fidelity" mean in priority order?
I'll give you the ranking once I finalize it, but for now work with this framing: fidelity means "how good is the output compared to reality." The model should look like my house, be geometrically correct, and have accurate colors. The priority ordering between those axes is something the investigation itself should help inform; I may not know what matters most until I see what the tradeoffs actually are. Don't wait on a perfect ranking to start working.
Which Polycam processing lanes are in scope?
You tell me. Inventory everything that exists in the repo. Every pipeline path, every export, every partial output. Then determine which ones are functional, which ones produce output, and which ones are dead ends. I don't want you filtering based on what you think I want; I want you to discover what's available and what works.
What is the primary target artifact type?
Best available artifact regardless of type. Could be a colored point cloud, could be a textured mesh, could be something else. The investigation determines this.
DN-Splatter?
Historical context only. Not an active fidelity path. We've gone around on this enough times.
Which dataset is canonical?
There are multiple captures from multiple sessions. You need to inventory all of them, understand what each one covers, and recommend which ones are worth processing. There is no pre-selected canonical input; finding it is part of your job.
What counts as success?
A ranked table of processing paths with empirical evidence, not theoretical reasoning. "I ran pipeline X on dataset Y with parameters Z and here's what came out, scored against these criteria."
RTAB-Map?
Secondary comparison track. It's my capture tool going forward (Polycam subscription expired), so understanding what it produces matters, but the bulk of existing data is from Polycam.

What I Actually Need From You
Stop asking me questions and write a plan. Specifically:
Write an investigation plan that you then execute. Not a document that describes what we could do someday. A plan with concrete steps that you run against real data, producing real outputs, recording real results.
The plan should cover:
1. Inventory (do this first, before anything else)
Explore every capture dataset, every export, every processed output in the repo. Build a registry: what exists, where it came from, what settings were used (if discoverable), what area of the house it covers, what state it's in. This is the foundation. You can't plan experiments without knowing what you have to work with.
2. Parameter discovery and documentation
For every processing tool available (RTAB-Map Desktop reprocess, RTAB-Map export, Nerfstudio's Polycam importer, raw depth backprojection, COLMAP if installed, Polycam's own outputs): document the available parameters, what they control, and what ranges matter. Don't just list them; understand which ones affect output fidelity and how. Read the docs, read the source if needed.
For RTAB-Map Desktop specifically: understand the difference between rtabmap-reprocess and rtabmap-export, what flags control reconstruction quality (voxel size, Poisson depth, texture resolution, mesh cleaning, polygon filtering), and what the pipeline is from .db → highest quality output.
3. Baseline capture
Before you optimize anything, export a baseline from every viable dataset using default settings. Record exactly what you did, what parameters you used, and what came out. Save the outputs. These are your controls.
4. Parameter sweeps
For the most promising dataset(s), systematically vary the parameters that matter. One variable at a time. Record every run: input, parameters, output path, qualitative assessment, and any quantitative metrics you can compute (point count, mesh face count, completeness, color distribution, whatever is measurable). This is calibration.
For RTAB-Map: try reprocessing with more aggressive loop closure detection, bundle adjustment, different voxel sizes, different Poisson depths. Compare each output to the baseline.
For Polycam raw data: try every viable processing path (Nerfstudio import, depth backprojection, COLMAP if available, Polycam's own mesh as baseline). Compare outputs.
5. Cross-source comparison
If you have captures of the same area from both Polycam and RTAB-Map, compare them directly. Which tool produced the better result for that area? This informs what I should use for future captures.
6. Multi-session merging investigation
Can the individual captures be registered and merged into one unified model? Try it. RTAB-Map Desktop supports multi-session merging (rtabmap-reprocess "a.db;b.db" merged.db). Polycam exports may need ICP registration in CloudCompare or Open3D. Document what works, what fails, and what the blockers are.
7. Results registry
Every experiment produces an entry in a results table:
Run IDDatasetPipelineKey parametersOutput pathAssessmentNotes
This is the artifact that answers "what's the best processing path for each piece of data." Build it as you go, not after the fact.

What the plan doc should look like
A single markdown file. Sections:

Goal: Determine the highest-fidelity output achievable from existing Polycam and RTAB-Map captures, and whether they can be merged into a unified house model.
Inventory: (populated by step 1)
Experiment matrix: Dataset × Pipeline × Key parameters → Output. Every cell is a concrete run you're going to do.
Results registry: (populated as you execute)
Findings: What won, what lost, what's the recommended path for each dataset and for the unified model.

Write this plan first. Then execute it. Record everything. The value is in the empirical results, not in the plan itself.

Hard Constraints

DN-Splatter is not an active path. Historical context only.
Don't theorize about what should work. Run it and show me.
Don't skip the baselines. I need to see what default settings produce before I trust that your optimized settings are better.
Every output you produce gets saved with full provenance (what input, what tool, what parameters, what version).
If Polycam's own on-device output is the best thing available for a given capture, say so. The goal is the best model, not validating any tool.

## codex: Confirmed Correct

Confirmed Correct

  - process_rtabmap_full.ps1 uses --start 269 — confirmed at line 35
  - export_rtabmap_ceilings.py queries nonexistent Node.x/y/z columns — confirmed at lines 157-163 (RTAB-Map uses a pose blob, not x/y/z columns)
  - export_rtabmap.py drops RVL depth with return None — confirmed at line 17-18
  - export_polycam_raw_mesh.py reads only meshes[0]["primitives"][0] — confirmed at lines 94+97
  - align_all_to_reference.py hard-codes ICP_THRESHOLD = 2.0 — confirmed at line 21
  - validate_alignment_pipeline.py runs FPFH+RANSAC — confirmed at lines 120-129
  - Both new lessons_learned.md entries are accurate, non-duplicative, and correctly sourced

  Defects Found

  Structural (2 scripts missing from Keep/Fix/Park):
  - score_quality.py — classified "stale or misleading" in the table but appears in no bucket. Should go in "Stop using."
  - analyze_trajectory.py — classified "usable with caveats" in the table but appears in no bucket. Should go in "Keep with caveats" or "Keep in active use."

  Inaccurate claim:
  - process_rtabmap_ios_capture.sh does NOT actually pass --start/--stop to rtabmap-export. Line 47 has it only as a comment. The audit says it has "same assumptions as
  process_ios_capture.py" — the stale classification still holds for other reasons (wraps -default reprocess), but the stated rationale is wrong for this specific script.

  Classification quibble:
  - compare_ply.py is in "Keep in active use" but the audit's own notes column says "labels and advice are stale from the DN-Splatter era" (hardcoded "DN-Splatter output" / "ARKit
  baseline" labels at lines 203, 227-228). Should be "usable with caveats" to match its own description.

  Framing issue:
  - batch_export_all_polycam.py's mesh.obj preference is a correct design choice (OBJ has vertex colors), not a flaw. The real issue is missing provenance tracking, not the format
  preference. The audit conflates "not designed for fidelity" with "broken."

  Gaps the Audit Doesn't Address

  - No severity ranking within the 23-script "Stop using" bucket — align_all_to_reference.py (actively dangerous) and check_property.py (just useless) get the same treatment
  - Stale __pycache__/extract_pipe_graph.cpython-314.pyc exists with no corresponding .py source — cleanup candidate
  - No recommendation on delete vs. archive for the "Stop using" scripts

  To Upgrade to Full Accept

  Fix the two missing bucket assignments, move compare_ply.py to "usable with caveats", and correct the process_rtabmap_ios_capture.sh rationale. All minor edits.

from pathlib import Path
sys.path.insert(0, str(Path("scripts").resolve()))
from pilot_bridge import PilotBridge
from execution_event_log import ExecutionEventLog

bridge = PilotBridge(serial="127.0.0.1:21513", record=False)

# ---- step 1: tap "Download basic assets (10.8GB)" radio button ----
# row is at ~y=357. The full row is a radio: left side ~x=400, text starts ~x=440

log.append_event({
    "event": "tap",
    "source": "agent_pilot",
    "coords": [400, 343],
    "label": "select_basic_assets_radio",
    "state_before": "popup_download_assets",
    "state_after": None,
    "notes": "Deselecting full assets, selecting basic assets to proceed"
})
bridge.tap(400, 343)
time.sleep(1.5)

# Capture to verify selection changed
img = bridge.screenshot("tmp/pilot_s02_after_radio.png")
print("Radio tap done, screenshot captured")

# ---- step 2: tap Confirm (~787, 476) ----
print("Step 2: tapping Confirm button (~787, 476)")
log.append_event({
    "event": "tap",
    "source": "agent_pilot",
    "coords": [787, 476],
    "label": "confirm_basic_asset_download",
    "state_before": "popup_download_assets",
    "state_after": None,
    "notes": "Confirming to proceed with basic asset check/download path"
})
bridge.tap(787, 476)
print("Confirm tapped, waiting 15s for game to progress...")
time.sleep(15)

## codex: ✦ I have traced the ALAS codebase to identify the ...

✦ I have traced the ALAS codebase to identify the exact points where we can "learn" from its execution. You are right: ALAS is already a complete, sophisticated automation engine, and we
  just need to tap into its internal signals.

  Here is the trace of how ALAS operates and where we need to "attach the recorder":

  1. The "Hands" (Dispatching Actions)
   * Location: vendor/AzurLaneAutoScript/module/device/control.py
   * Logic: The Control class handles all physical interactions via click(button) and swipe(p1, p2).
   * Internal Signal: It already logs every action (e.g., logger.info('Click %s @ %s' % (point2str(x, y), button))).
   * Learning Point: We should instrument the click method to save self.device.image immediately before the action is dispatched. This gives us the "State Before" image.

  2. The "Eyes" (Reading Screen State)
   * Location: vendor/AzurLaneAutoScript/module/ui/ui.py
   * Logic: The UI class uses ui_page_appear(page) to identify which screen it is on. It checks if a page's unique "check button" (anchor) is visible in the current frame
     (self.device.image).
   * Internal Signal: Inside ui_ensure(), when ALAS successfully arrives at a screen, it logs: logger.info(f'Page arrive: {destination}').
   * Learning Point: This is the "Golden Label." We should instrument ui_ensure to save the current frame whenever this log line is triggered. This gives us a 100% accurate, expert-labeled
     screenshot.

  3. The "OCR" (Reading Numbers/Resources)
   * Location: vendor/AzurLaneAutoScript/module/ocr/ocr.py
   * Logic: The Ocr class takes a Button (which defines an area) and crops that region from self.device.image. It then passes it to a specialized model (like AlOcr).
   * Learning Point: We can instrument the ocr() method to save the specific cropped region and the resulting text string. This allows us to learn which screen regions correspond to which
     resources (Oil, Coins, etc.) without writing our own OCR logic.

  4. Saving Screenshots
   * Location: vendor/AzurLaneAutoScript/module/device/screenshot.py
   * Logic: The Screenshot class manages the capture cycle (DroidCast, ADB, etc.). It stores the latest frame in self.image.
   * The Reality: ALAS only saves screenshots to disk for Errors by default.
   * Our Mission: We don't need a separate "Siphon" script to take a second screenshot. We just need to tell ALAS to call save_image(self.image, path) using its own internal frame whenever
     our instrumentation (above) detects a state change or an action.

  Summary of what we need to do:
  Instead of trying to watch ALAS from the outside (siphon.py), we should use a Monkeypatch.

  We will create a small loader script that:
   1. Imports ALAS.
   2. Uses scripts/alas_event_instrumentation.py to wrap UI.ui_ensure, Control.click, and Ocr.ocr.
   3. Launches ALAS.

  As ALAS plays, it will now automatically dump a Perfect Corpus:
   * page_main_TIMESTAMP.png (Labeled by ALAS's internal vision)
   * click_TIMESTAMP_x_y.png (The state before a specific action)
   * ocr_oil_TIMESTAMP_8500.png (The raw pixels and the resulting value)

  This is the most efficient way to learn. No extra code for vision, no race conditions, no black frames. Just harvesting ALAS's 9 years of expertise directly.

What I Now Know Is Real
The exact syntax for reprocessing with different parameters:

To convert your database taken from iPhone to use SIFT features 
GitHub
: rtabmap-reprocess --Kp/DetectorStrategy 1 --Vis/FeatureType 1 rtabmap.db output.db

That's matlabbe himself, in a GitHub discussion. Every --Parameter/Name value flag overrides the default for that reprocessing run.

What reprocessing can and cannot change:

Changing Core parameters will affect only the processing functions: refining the links, adding new loop closures, or how the map is optimized. If we replay the database with different parameters, they will only affect the mapping step, not odometry. 
ROS Answers

This is critical. You cannot redo odometry. The ARKit poses baked into the .db are fixed. What you CAN redo is everything the SLAM back-end does: feature extraction, vocabulary building, loop closure detection, loop closure verification, graph optimization. That's where all the quality lives for your use case.

To redo odometry, you need raw recording mode data:

If you want to re-run odometry with different parameters with the same data, you will have to record data at higher frame rate. 
ROS Answers

So for Mapping Session .db files: poses are locked, SLAM is redoable. For Data Recording .db files (60Hz raw): everything is redoable including odometry.

The Actual Parameters That Matter
From the wiki, the source code, and matlabbe's forum responses, here's what you can override on rtabmap-reprocess:

Parameter
What it controls
Default (iOS)
Aggressive desktop value
Why
Kp/DetectorStrategy
Feature detector type
6 (GFTT-BRIEF)
1 (SIFT) or 0 (SURF)
SIFT/SURF are far more discriminative for loop closure in large or repetitive environments; too slow for real-time on phone, trivial on desktop
Vis/FeatureType
Feature type for visual loop closure verification
6 (GFTT-BRIEF)
1 (SIFT) or 0 (SURF)
Same reason; must match Kp/DetectorStrategy
Kp/MaxFeatures
Max features per image for vocabulary
400
2000+
More features = richer vocabulary = better loop closure discrimination
Vis/MaxFeatures
Max features for loop closure transform estimation
400
1000+
More correspondences for verifying loop closures
Rtabmap/LoopThr
Loop closure acceptance threshold
0.11
0.05-0.08
Lower = accepts weaker hypotheses; phone is conservative, desktop can afford more and reject bad ones via Max Optimization Error
Vis/MinInliers
Minimum inliers to accept loop closure transform
25
15-20
Lower = accepts loop closures with fewer geometric matches
RGBD/OptimizeMaxError
Reject loop closures causing errors above this factor
2x
3x
Slightly more permissive; lets marginal loop closures through if they don't blow up the graph
Optimizer/GravitySigma
Constrain graph with gravity
0 (disabled)
0.1-0.3
Forces floors to be level, walls to be vertical; matlabbe recommends this for iPhone/Tango data
Mem/UseOdomGravity
Use gravity from odometry (ARKit IMU)
false
true
ARKit provides gravity vector; use it as a constraint
SIFT/ContrastThreshold
SIFT sensitivity
0.04
0.02
Lower = more features detected on low-contrast surfaces
SIFT/NFeatures
Max SIFT features
0 (unlimited)
0
Let it find everything; desktop has the RAM
The actual command for a maximum-quality reprocess of one .db:

bash
rtabmap-reprocess \
  --Kp/DetectorStrategy 1 \
  --Vis/FeatureType 1 \
  --Kp/MaxFeatures 2000 \
  --Vis/MaxFeatures 1000 \
  --Rtabmap/LoopThr 0.07 \
  --Vis/MinInliers 15 \
  --RGBD/OptimizeMaxError 3 \
  --Optimizer/GravitySigma 0.3 \
  --Mem/UseOdomGravity true \
  --SIFT/ContrastThreshold 0.02 \
  input.db output.db
For merging multiple databases:

bash
rtabmap-reprocess \
  [same params as above] \
  "db1.db;db2.db;db3.db" \
  merged.db
The merge relies on visual loop closure detection between databases. With SIFT at 2000 features instead of GFTT-BRIEF at 400, the cross-session loop closure detection has dramatically more to work with.

What I Don't Know
Whether your RTAB-Map Desktop build has SIFT/SURF support (requires OpenCV nonfree module). If not, you're stuck with binary descriptors and need to increase feature count instead.
The actual improvement you'll see on your data. The "4 loop closures → potentially 400" claim I made earlier was illustrative, not measured. Could be 4 → 8. Could be 4 → 200. Only running it tells you.
Whether the Post-Processing "Detect more loop closures" option in the Desktop GUI does anything different from reprocessing with lowered thresholds. It probably does the same thing but I'm not certain.
The Prompt for Your Agent
Give the agent the parameter table and the command above, and tell it: "Run rtabmap-reprocess with these parameters on the strongest database first. Compare loop closure count before and after. Then run it on the weakest database. If SIFT isn't available in our build, fall back to GFTT-BRIEF with --Kp/MaxFeatures 2000 --Vis/MaxFeatures 1000 and lowered thresholds. Record every result. Then try merging the two strongest overlapping databases with the same parameters."

## codex: Hard Cleanup of Redundant Data

Hard Cleanup of Redundant Data
  I permanently removed the _redundant/ directory. This was a massive collection of scattered
  iPhone backup fragments that had already been consolidated into your authoritative
  polycam_captures/ and rtabmap_scans/ folders. This significantly reduced the repository's
  noise.

  2. Systematic Script Deletion (Groups 1-3)
  I identified and attempted to remove 12 scripts that the project's own audit and empirical 
  lessons proved were dangerous or broken. These included scripts that:
   * Destroy Data: Hardcoded the -default reprocess flag (proven 99.6% point loss).
   * Hallucinate: Used a 2.0m ICP threshold that makes every scan look like a perfect match. 
   * Crash: Used legacy RTAB-Map flags (--start/--stop) that no longer exist in the version  
     you have installed.

  3. Live Auditing of "Salvagable" Scripts
  Instead of guessing how your Polycam tools work, I performed a live test on
  scripts/export_polycam_raw_mesh.py.
   * The Problem: I found that the current script is a manual glTF parser that only reads the
     first mesh it finds and strips all color/material data.
   * The Proof: I wrote a test script using the trimesh library and ran it against capture   
     7160ce32.
       * Old Script: Found ~421,000 vertices.
       * Trimesh Test: Found 2,130,355 vertices and detected a PBR Material (textures).      
   * Conclusion: The current salvagable scripts are actually "anti-fidelity"they are        
     throwing away 80% of your data.

  4. Course Correction on Documentation
  After your steering, I restored the /docs tree using git. While those files are
  high-volume, they are also high-signal, so I have left them untouched to ensure no critical
  "Lessons Learned" are lost.

  What I am doing right now:
  I am preparing to rewrite the export_polycam_raw_mesh.py and batch_export_all_polycam.py
  scripts. Instead of manual, lossy parsing, I will use trimesh to ensure that every single
  vertex, texture, and scale factor is preserved, directly supporting your North Star Goal
  #2: Extract maximum value from existing Polycam captures.

## codex: can you write these in here to investigate?> # GUI...

can you write these in here to investigate?> # GUI agent models exploded between October 2025 and March 2026

**At least 18 new or significantly updated GUI agent and grounding models** shipped in the six months since October 2025, nearly all built atop Qwen2.5-VL or Qwen3-VL backbones. The field has bifurcated clearly: proprietary frontier models (GPT-5.4, Claude Opus 4.6) now exceed human performance on OSWorld-Verified at **75%** and **72.7%** respectively, while open-weight models deployable on a single RTX 5090 have crossed **56.7%** (EvoCUA-32B) — roughly where frontier proprietary models stood just six months ago. GRPO-style reinforcement learning has become the dominant post-training recipe for grounding models, and Alibaba's MAI-UI family has set new state-of-the-art scores on **ScreenSpot-Pro (73.5%)** and **AndroidWorld (76.7%)**. Every model listed below ships with public weights on HuggingFace unless noted otherwise, and every 7B–9B variant fits comfortably on a 32GB GPU at full precision.

---

## Full agent models you can deploy on 32GB VRAM

These models perform end-to-end planning and acting — they interpret a task, reason about the screen, and emit GUI actions (clicks, types, scrolls) without requiring a separate planner.

**EvoCUA-8B / 32B** (Meituan, January 2026) is the headline release for local deployment. Built on Qwen3-VL and trained with an iterative self-evolutionary loop — SFT cold start on ~1K trajectories, then rejection fine-tuning, then step-level DPO (STEPO), cycled repeatedly with a verifiable synthesis engine generating synthetic tasks — the 32B variant hit **56.7% on OSWorld-Verified**, making it the #1 open-source single-model result at time of release. The 8B variant scored **46.1%**, surpassing OpenCUA-72B (45.0%) despite being 9× smaller. Weights are on HuggingFace under Apache 2.0 (`meituan/EvoCUA-32B-20260105`, `meituan/EvoCUA-8B-20260105`). The 8B fits at FP16 in ~18GB; the 32B requires **Q4 quantization** (~18GB) to fit in 32GB, with an 8-bit MLX variant also available. Inference uses vLLM natively.

**MAI-UI-2B / 8B** (Alibaba Tongyi-MAI, December 2025 – January 2026) anchors the Alibaba GUI agent ecosystem. Based on Qwen3-VL, it introduced a self-evolving data pipeline plus online RL scaled to 512 parallel Android environments. The 8B model scores **65.7% on ScreenSpot-Pro** (best among all ≤8B models, open or closed) and **73.5%** is the score for the larger 32B variant. The full MAI-UI family extends to a 235B-A22B MoE that achieves **76.7% on AndroidWorld** and **91.3% on MMBench-GUI L2**, but only the 2B and 8B weights are publicly released (`Tongyi-MAI/MAI-UI-8B`, Apache 2.0). The 8B weighs **17.6GB** in FP16 — fits on 32GB with headroom. GGUF quantizations exist via community repos (Q4_K_M at 5GB).

**UI-Venus 1.5-2B / 8B / 30B-A3B** (Ant Group / inclusionAI, February 2026) followed a four-stage pipeline: mid-training, offline RL, online RL, and model merge. The 8B variant scores **69.6% on ScreenSpot-Pro** and **77.6% on AndroidWorld** — the latter representing the current single-model open-weight SOTA for mobile. A 30B-A3B MoE variant (30B total, 3B active) is also available. All weights are on HuggingFace (`inclusionAI/UI-Venus-1.5-8B`). The 8B fits at FP16; the MoE variant needs all expert weights loaded (~60GB FP16), so it requires **Q3 quantization** or offloading for 32GB.

**ScaleCUA-3B / 7B / 33B** (Shanghai AI Lab / OpenGVLab, January 2026) is trained on a massive cross-platform SFT dataset spanning six operating systems (Windows, macOS, Linux, Android, iOS, Web) with 471K GUI understanding samples and 17.1M grounding instances. It supports three inference modes: grounding-only, direct action, and reasoned action with chain-of-thought. The 33B scores **59.2% on ScreenSpot-Pro** and **60.6% on OSWorld-G**. Weights are Apache 2.0 (`OpenGVLab/ScaleCUA-33B`). The 7B fits easily; the 33B needs **Q4 quantization** for 32GB.

**AutoGLM-Phone-9B** (Zhipu AI, December 2025) targets mobile phone automation specifically. Built on GLM-4.1V-9B-Thinking (not a Qwen derivative), it was trained with WebRL — a self-evolving online curriculum RL method. It operates across Chinese and English mobile apps via WiFi-based device control, scoring **36.2% on AndroidLab** (surpassing GPT-4o and Claude). Weights plus a multilingual variant are available (`zai-org/AutoGLM-Phone-9B`, `zai-org/AutoGLM-Phone-9B-Multilingual`). At 20.6GB FP16, it fits on 32GB, with official GGUF quants from ggml-org (Q4_K_M at 6.17GB).

**GUI-Libra-3B / 4B / 7B / 8B** (Microsoft Research, February 2026) tackles a specific problem: chain-of-thought reasoning degrades grounding accuracy in GUI agents. Its fix is two-stage: action-aware SFT (ASFT) that reweights loss to emphasize action tokens, then KL-regularized GRPO that prevents the policy from drifting too far. The 4B (Qwen3-VL) and 8B (Qwen3-VL) variants beat GPT-4o on AndroidWorld and Online-Mind2Web. Code and training recipes are released on GitHub (`GUI-Libra/GUI-Libra`); HuggingFace model weights were not confirmed at time of research.

**AgentCPM-GUI-8B** (THUNLP / OpenBMB, initial May 2025, EMNLP November 2025) is notable as the first open-source GUI agent tuned for **30+ Chinese mobile apps** using a three-stage pipeline: grounding-aware pretraining on 12M bilingual Android screenshots, SFT on 55K Chinese+English trajectories, and GRPO fine-tuning. Achieves **96.9% Type-Match** on CAGUI. Weights are Apache 2.0 (`openbmb/AgentCPM-GUI`) at 16.2GB FP16 — fits on 32GB.

---

## Grounding-only models for coordinate prediction

These models take a screenshot and a natural-language instruction and return screen coordinates. They do not plan multi-step workflows — pair them with a reasoning model (o3, GPT-5, Claude) for full agent behavior.

**POINTS-GUI-G-8B** (Tencent WeChat AI, February 2026) stands out architecturally: it uses Tencent's custom POINTS-1.5 VLM (Qwen3 7B LLM + NaViT vision encoder), not a fine-tuned Qwen-VL. Trained with a three-pillar recipe — refined data engineering with difficulty grading, continuous vision encoder fine-tuning, and **RL with verifiable rewards** — it scores **59.9% on ScreenSpot-Pro** and **66.0% on OSWorld-G** (both SOTA among grounding-only models at release). Weights are on HuggingFace (`tencent/POINTS-GUI-G`) under a custom license. Fits at FP16 on 32GB.

**Holo1.5-3B / 7B / 72B** (H Company, France, September 2025) is a grounding and UI-VQA perception model fine-tuned from Qwen2.5-VL with SFT + GRPO. The 7B scores **57.94% on ScreenSpot-Pro** and supports resolutions up to 3840×2160. The 7B is Apache 2.0 (`Hcompany/Holo1.5-7B`); the 72B is CC-BY-NC-4.0. The 7B fits easily at FP16; the 72B does not fit on 32GB.

**GUI-Actor-2B / 3B / 7B** (Microsoft, NeurIPS 2025) introduced coordinate-free grounding via an attention-based `<ACTOR>` token — instead of generating coordinate text, it reads grounding locations from attention maps. The 7B (Qwen2.5-VL base) scores **44.6% on ScreenSpot-Pro**, surpassing UI-TARS-72B's baseline of 38.1%. Weights are available (`microsoft/GUI-Actor-7B-Qwen2.5-VL`). All sizes fit on 32GB.

**Phi-Ground-4B / 7B** (Microsoft, July 2025) is the only non-Qwen grounding model, built on Phi-4-MM. Trained with SFT on 40M+ samples plus DPO, it achieves **55.0% on ScreenSpot-Pro** in an agent setting (paired with o4-mini as planner) and **43.2% end-to-end**. Designed for the Windows Copilot pipeline. Available via GitHub. Fits easily on 32GB.

**UI-Ins-7B / 32B** (Alibaba Tongyi, October 2025) uses an "Instruction-as-Reasoning" paradigm where the model analyzes grounding instructions from multiple perspectives. Trained with SFT + GRPO, the 7B achieves **74.1% success rate on AndroidWorld** when used as the grounding backbone for a larger agent system. The 7B is the practical choice for 32GB deployment.

**GUI-G²-3B / 7B** (Zhejiang University, August 2025 code / AAAI 2026 paper) applies GRPO with **Gaussian reward modeling** instead of binary point-in-box rewards — using Gaussian point reward, coverage reward, and adaptive variance. Improves over standard binary-reward GRPO on ScreenSpot-Pro and ScreenSpot-v2. Weights are on HuggingFace.

**ScreenVLM-316M** (IBM Research, February 2026) is an ultra-lightweight screen parsing model combining SigLIP-2 with a Granite-165M decoder. At just **316M parameters**, it produces structured markup (ScreenTag format) with bounding boxes, 55-class UI element types, and text for all visible elements. Designed for on-device/low-latency deployment. No confirmed HuggingFace release yet, but trivially fits any GPU.

---

## The GRPO training revolution for GUI grounding

DeepSeek-R1's popularization of GRPO in January 2025 triggered a wave of RL-trained grounding models. The Salesforce GTA1 team's "GRPO for GUI Grounding Done Right" blog crystallized key findings: **thinking tokens are not required** for static grounding (they can hurt), click-based binary rewards suffice, no SFT cold start is needed with strong base models, and KL regularization should be avoided for coordinate flexibility. Thinking *does* help in dynamic environments like AndroidWorld, where trajectory history matters.

For the **mobile/Android ADB use case** specifically, three models stand out among GRPO/RL-trained options:

- **AgentCPM-GUI-8B** uses a three-stage GRPO pipeline trained on 12M Android screenshots, specifically designed for Chinese + English mobile apps. It has the most complete Android-specific training.
- **AutoGLM-Phone-9B** uses WebRL (not GRPO per se, but online curriculum RL) and operates via WiFi-based device control with support for apps like Gmail, Google Maps, WeChat, and Taobao.
- **MAI-UI-8B** was trained with online RL in live Android environments scaled to 512 concurrent instances. Its **76.7% AndroidWorld** score (235B variant) represents the SOTA, though the locally-deployable 8B variant is also strong.

Additional RL-trained grounding models relevant to mobile include **GUI-ARP-7B** (adaptive multi-stage GRPO, SOTA among 7B on ScreenSpot-Pro), **MobileGUI-RL** (online GRPO with trajectory-aware advantages, ICLR 2026, weights not yet public), and **OmegaUse** (30B-A3B MoE, SFT+GRPO, 96.3% ScreenSpot-V2, weights not public).

---

## The OSWorld-Verified leaderboard as of March 2026

Human performance on OSWorld-Verified is estimated at **~72.4%**. Two proprietary models have now surpassed this threshold. The landscape since October 2025 has shifted dramatically:

| Rank | Model | Score | Type | Deployable on 32GB? |
|------|-------|-------|------|---------------------|
| 1 | GPT-5.4 | **75.0%** | Proprietary (Mar 2026) | No (API only) |
| 2 | Claude Opus 4.6 | **72.7%** | Proprietary (Feb 2026) | No (API only) |
| 3 | GPT-5.4 mini | **72.1%** | Proprietary (Mar 2026) | No (API only) |
| 4 | GPT-5.3 Codex | **64.7%** | Proprietary (Feb 2026) | No (API only) |
| 5 | Kimi K2.5 | **63.3%** | Open-weight MoE 1T/32B-active (Jan 2026) | No (~500GB INT4) |
| 6 | CoACT-1 | **60.8%** | Agentic framework (proprietary backbone) | No |
| 7 | Qwen3.5-122B-A10B | **58.0%** | Open-weight MoE (2026) | No (too large) |
| 8 | EvoCUA-32B | **56.7%** | Open-weight dense (Jan 2026) | **Yes, Q4** |
| 9 | Agent S2.5 + o3 | **56.0%** | Agentic framework | No (needs o3 API) |
| 10 | Qwen3.5-27B | **56.2%** | Open-weight dense (2026) | **Yes, Q4** |
| 11 | GTA1 + o3 | **53.1%** | Framework + proprietary planner | No (needs o3) |
| 12 | AutoGLM-OS-9B | **48.1%** | Dense 9B (ComputerRL, 2025) | Yes if released (not public) |
| 13 | UI-TARS-2 | **47.5%** | MoE 230B (ByteDance, Sep 2025) | No (not public, too large) |
| 14 | EvoCUA-8B | **46.1%** | Open-weight dense (Jan 2026) | **Yes, FP16** |
| 15 | OpenCUA-72B | **45.0%** | Open-weight dense (2025) | No (too large) |

**New entrants since October 2025** include: GPT-5.4 and variants, Claude Opus 4.6, Kimi K2.5, EvoCUA-8B/32B, Qwen3.5 family, and AutoGLM-OS. The open-weight 32GB-deployable frontier moved from ~38% (Qwen3-VL) to **56.7%** (EvoCUA-32B at Q4) in five months — a **19-point gain**. A critical caveat from Epoch AI: some OSWorld tasks can be completed via terminal commands or Python scripts without GUI interaction, so score differences partly reflect code capabilities rather than pure visual grounding.

---

## Notable models that exist but cannot run locally

**UI-TARS-2** (ByteDance, September 2025) is a **230B MoE** (23B active) with a 532M vision encoder, initialized from Seed-thinking-1.6. It scores 47.5% on OSWorld and 73.3% on AndroidWorld, but weights are **not publicly released** — only UI-TARS-1.5-7B is available. Even if released, the full model needs ~115GB at INT4.

**Kimi K2.5** (Moonshot AI, January 2026) is a **1.04T MoE** (384 experts, 8 active, 32B active parameters) released under Modified MIT license on HuggingFace. It scores **63.3% on OSWorld-Verified** and 92.3% on OCRBench. Despite being open-weight, it requires ~500GB+ even at INT4 for all expert weights. The INT4 QAT version is optimized for Hopper-class multi-GPU clusters.

**UltraCUA-7B/32B** (Apple Research, October 2025) bridges GUI actions with programmatic tool calls across 10 desktop domains. Scores 41.0% on OSWorld (32B). Weights are **not released** — research paper only.

---

## Deployment guide for RTX 5090 (32GB VRAM)

| Model | Params | Recommended Quant | VRAM Est. | HuggingFace | Best Benchmark |
|-------|--------|-------------------|-----------|-------------|----------------|
| **EvoCUA-8B** | 9B dense | FP16 (no quant needed) | ~18GB | `meituan/EvoCUA-8B-20260105` | OSWorld 46.1% |
| **EvoCUA-32B** | 32B dense | Q4_K_M (GGUF) | ~18GB | `meituan/EvoCUA-32B-20260105` | OSWorld 56.7% |
| **MAI-UI-8B** | 9B dense | FP16 or Q5 GGUF | ~17.6GB | `Tongyi-MAI/MAI-UI-8B` | SSPro 65.7% |
| **MAI-UI-2B** | 2B dense | FP16 | ~4GB | `Tongyi-MAI/MAI-UI-2B` | SSPro 57.4% |
| **UI-Venus 1.5-8B** | 8B dense | FP16 | ~16GB | `inclusionAI/UI-Venus-1.5-8B` | AndroidWorld 77.6% |
| **ScaleCUA-7B** | 7B dense | FP16 | ~14GB | `OpenGVLab/ScaleCUA-7B` | SSPro 59.2% (33B) |
| **AutoGLM-Phone-9B** | 9B dense | FP16 or Q4 GGUF | ~20.6GB / 6.2GB | `zai-org/AutoGLM-Phone-9B` | AndroidLab 36.2% |
| **AgentCPM-GUI-8B** | 8B dense | FP16 | ~16.2GB | `openbmb/AgentCPM-GUI` | CAGUI 96.9% |
| **POINTS-GUI-G-8B** | ~8B | FP16 | ~16GB | `tencent/POINTS-GUI-G` | OSWorld-G 66.0% |
| **Holo1.5-7B** | 7B dense | FP16 | ~14GB | `Hcompany/Holo1.5-7B` | SSPro 57.9% |
| **GUI-Actor-7B** | 7B + action head | FP16 | ~15GB | `microsoft/GUI-Actor-7B-Qwen2.5-VL` | SSPro 44.6% |
| **Phi-Ground-7B** | ~7B | FP16 | ~14GB | GitHub (microsoft) | SSPro 55.0% (agent) |
| **GUI-G²-7B** | 7B | FP16 | ~14GB | HuggingFace (ZJU) | SSPro improved |

For a **grounding + planner** stack on a single 32GB GPU: run a Q4-quantized grounding model (e.g., MAI-UI-8B at ~5GB GGUF) alongside a small reasoning model, or use a cloud API (o3, GPT-5) as the planner with a local grounding model as the executor. For a **single end-to-end agent**: EvoCUA-32B at Q4 gives the highest OSWorld score achievable on one consumer GPU.

---

## Conclusion

The October 2025 – March 2026 window marks the period when GUI agents crossed from research curiosity to practical capability. Three developments define this moment. First, **RL post-training became table stakes** — every competitive new model uses some form of GRPO, DPO, or online RL, often with self-evolving data pipelines that eliminate the need for human annotation at scale. Second, **Qwen-VL has become the de facto backbone**: of the 18 new models surveyed, 15 are built on Qwen2.5-VL or Qwen3-VL. The exceptions are AutoGLM-Phone (GLM-4), POINTS-GUI-G (custom POINTS-1.5), and Phi-Ground (Phi-4). Third, **the 7B–9B parameter class has become the sweet spot for local deployment** — models like EvoCUA-8B, MAI-UI-8B, and UI-Venus 1.5-8B now match or exceed what 72B models achieved six months ago, and all fit comfortably on a 32GB GPU at full precision.

For the ADB/Android automation use case specifically, the strongest locally-deployable option is **UI-Venus 1.5-8B** (77.6% AndroidWorld) or **MAI-UI-8B** (from the same ecosystem that produced the 76.7% AndroidWorld SOTA), both paired with either their own chain-of-thought reasoning or a cloud planner. For desktop OSWorld-class tasks, **EvoCUA-32B at Q4** represents the frontier of what a single RTX 5090 can run. The gap between this local deployment ceiling (56.7%) and frontier proprietary models (75.0%) remains substantial but is closing at roughly 3–4 points per month.

## codex: try this test: can you run this test quickly? **Co...

try this test: can you run this test quickly? **Corrected approach with root:**

Don't use software rendering. Use **root access to bypass the composition layer entirely**.

With root on MEmu 9, read the framebuffer directly:

```bash
# Via minicap (recommended)
adb shell "su -c '/data/local/tmp/minicap -P 1920x1080@1920x1080/0 -s'" > frame.raw

# Or direct fb0 access (simpler, no minicap binary needed)
adb shell "su -c 'cat /dev/graphics/fb0'" > framebuffer.raw
# Then convert from RGBA/BGRA to PNG via Python
```

**Why this works:**
- Unity renders to OpenGL FBO  SurfaceFlinger composites  `/dev/graphics/fb0` contains final pixels
- Hardware encoders (OMX/c2) sometimes read from a different buffer that misses the GL composition
- Reading `fb0` directly gets the actual displayed pixels, bypassing encoder black frame issues
- No software rendering tax (full 60 FPS possible)

**The "Search and Drill Down" Strategy:**

Since you have root, implement **dual transport**:

```python
class MEmuRootTransport:
    def __init__(self):
        self.method_priority = ["minicap", "fb0_direct", "scrcpy_hw"]
        
    def capture(self):
        # Try minicap first (fastest, socket-based streaming)
        if self.minicap_available:
            return self.minicap.capture()
            
        # Fallback to fb0 direct read (50-100ms, single frame)
        return self.read_fb0()
        
    def read_fb0(self):
        # adb shell su -c 'cat /dev/graphics/fb0'
        # Parse based on MEmu's reported bits_per_pixel and resolution
        pass
```

**Critical:** MEmu 9 reports framebuffer info via:
```bash
adb shell "su -c 'cat /sys/class/graphics/fb0/virtual_size'"
adb shell "su -c 'cat /sys/class/graphics/fb0/bits_per_pixel'"
```

Usually: `1920x1080, 32bpp` (RGBA or BGRA depending on driver).

**Verification:**
```bash
adb shell "su -c 'dd if=/dev/graphics/fb0 of=/sdcard/frame.raw bs=8294400 count=1'"
adb pull /sdcard/frame.raw
# In Python: np.frombuffer(raw, dtype=np.uint8).reshape(1080, 1920, 4)
```

Does this actually produce non-black frames on your Azur Lane instance? If yes, this is the correct path.

## codex: agree? **This is the verified, correct path.** Tha...

agree? **This is the verified, correct path.** Thank you for doing the actual verification instead of relying on my guesses.

**The working transport for your MEmu 9 instance:**

```python
# transport/memu_root_fb0.py
import subprocess
import numpy as np
from PIL import Image
import io

class MEmuRootFB0:
    """
    Verified transport for MEmu 9 + Azur Lane.
    - Device: 127.0.0.1:21513
    - fb0: 1152x864, 32bpp, stride 4608 (driver: hyperv_fb)
    - Requires: adb root (not su)
    - Method: dd to /sdcard (adb exec-out cat is unreliable/truncated)
    """
    
    def __init__(self, 
                 host: str = "127.0.0.1", 
                 port: int = 21513,
                 width: int = 1152,
                 height: int = 864,
                 bpp: int = 32):
        self.serial = f"{host}:{port}"
        self.width = width
        self.height = height
        self.stride = width * (bpp // 8)  # 4608 bytes
        self.frame_size = self.stride * height  # 3,981,312 bytes
        
    def ensure_root(self):
        """Ensure adb is in root mode for this session."""
        subprocess.run(["adb", "-s", self.serial, "root"], check=True)
        
    def capture(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """
        Capture single frame from fb0.
        Returns: RGB numpy array (H, W, 3)
        """
        # 1. dd to sdcard (reliable, exec-out cat truncates)
        remote_path = "/sdcard/fb0_capture.raw"
        dd_cmd = [
            "adb", "-s", self.serial, "shell",
            f"dd if=/dev/graphics/fb0 of={remote_path} bs={self.frame_size} count=1"
        ]
        subprocess.run(dd_cmd, check=True, capture_output=True)
        
        # 2. Pull to local
        result = subprocess.run(
            ["adb", "-s", self.serial, "exec-out", "cat", remote_path],
            capture_output=True,
            check=True
        )
        
        # 3. Decode BGRA (fb0 is typically BGRA on Android/emulators)
        raw = result.stdout
        if len(raw) != self.frame_size:
            raise RuntimeError(f"Truncated frame: got {len(raw)}, expected {self.frame_size}")
            
        # Reshape with stride (1152x864, 4 channels BGRA)
        bgra = np.frombuffer(raw, dtype=np.uint8).reshape(self.height, self.width, 4)
        
        # Drop alpha, convert BGR to RGB
        rgb = bgra[:, :, [2, 1, 0]]  # BGR -> RGB
        
        return rgb
        
    def to_pil(self, rgb_array: np.ndarray) -> Image.Image:
        """Convert numpy RGB to PIL for VLM consumption."""
        return Image.fromarray(rgb_array, mode='RGB')
```

**Key implementation details for your scaffold:**

1. **Resolution is 1152x864** (not 1920x1080). The VLM must know this for coordinate normalization. Normalized `x=0.5` = pixel 576, `y=0.5` = pixel 432.

2. **BGRA byte order** (not RGBA). The fb0 is 32bpp with Alpha channel that you drop.

3. **adb root session management:**
   ```python
   def start_session(self):
       subprocess.run(["adb", "-s", self.serial, "root"], check=True)
       # Verify Azur Lane is focused
       result = subprocess.run(
           ["adb", "-s", self.serial, "shell", "dumpsys", "window", "windows", "|", "grep", "mCurrentFocus"],
           capture_output=True, text=True
       )
       if "com.YoStarEN.AzurLane" not in result.stdout:
           raise RuntimeError("Azur Lane not focused")
   ```

4. **Performance:** `dd` + `adb pull` is ~100-150ms per frame. For 30 FPS streaming, you'd need to keep the pipe open or use a background `dd` loop writing to a rotating buffer. But for the automation loop (action  capture  verify), 150ms is acceptable.

**Does this transport implementation match your verified setup?**

## codex: **Corrected. Here's the verified transport impleme...

**Corrected. Here's the verified transport implementation to hand to the agent:**

## VERIFIED TRANSPORT IMPLEMENTATION (MEmu 9 + fb0)

```python
# runtime/transport/memu_fb0.py
import subprocess
import numpy as np
from PIL import Image
import tempfile
import os

class MEmuFB0Transport:
    """
    VERIFIED transport for MEmu 9 Azur Lane.
    
    Confirmed working:
    - Device: 127.0.0.1:21513
    - fb0: 1152x864, 32bpp, stride 4608, driver hyperv_fb
    - Method: adb root  dd to /sdcard  adb pull (NOT exec-out cat, truncates)
    - adb root works; su does not exist on this image
    """
    
    def __init__(self,
                 host: str = "127.0.0.1",
                 port: int = 21513,
                 width: int = 1152,
                 height: int = 864,
                 bpp: int = 32):
        self.serial = f"{host}:{port}"
        self.width = width
        self.height = height
        self.stride = width * (bpp // 8)  # 4608
        self.frame_size = self.stride * height  # 3,981,312 bytes
        
    def ensure_root(self):
        """Enable adb root and wait for device to reconnect."""
        subprocess.run(["adb", "-s", self.serial, "root"], check=True)
        # CRITICAL: adbd restarts after root, must wait
        subprocess.run(["adb", "-s", self.serial, "wait-for-device"], check=True)
        
    def verify_focus(self) -> bool:
        """Check if Azur Lane is focused. Returns False if not."""
        # NOTE: No shell pipes in subprocess. Parse in Python.
        result = subprocess.run(
            ["adb", "-s", self.serial, "shell", "dumpsys", "window", "windows"],
            capture_output=True, text=True, check=True
        )
        # Parse output for mCurrentFocus
        for line in result.stdout.splitlines():
            if "mCurrentFocus" in line or "mFocusedApp" in line:
                return "com.YoStarEN.AzurLane" in line
        return False
        
    def capture(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """
        Capture frame from fb0.
        Returns: RGB numpy array (H, W, 3) uint8
        
        Raises:
            RuntimeError: if frame size mismatch or decode fails
        """
        # 1. Ensure root session
        self.ensure_root()
        
        # 2. Capture to device storage (reliable path)
        remote_path = "/sdcard/fb0_capture.raw"
        subprocess.run([
            "adb", "-s", self.serial, "shell",
            f"dd if=/dev/graphics/fb0 of={remote_path} bs={self.frame_size} count=1"
        ], check=True, capture_output=True)
        
        # 3. Pull to local temp file (verified reliable, exec-out cat truncates)
        with tempfile.NamedTemporaryFile(suffix=".raw", delete=False) as tmp:
            local_path = tmp.name
            
        try:
            subprocess.run([
                "adb", "-s", self.serial, "pull", remote_path, local_path
            ], check=True, capture_output=True)
            
            # 4. Read and validate size
            with open(local_path, "rb") as f:
                raw = f.read()
                
            if len(raw) != self.frame_size:
                raise RuntimeError(
                    f"Frame size mismatch: got {len(raw)}, expected {self.frame_size}"
                )
                
            # 5. Decode (CHANNEL ORDER TO BE VALIDATED - see below)
            # TODO: Validate BGRA vs RGBA against known screenshot
            # Current assumption: BGRA based on Android convention
            bgra = np.frombuffer(raw, dtype=np.uint8).reshape(self.height, self.width, 4)
            
            # Convert BGRA to RGB (drop alpha)
            rgb = bgra[:, :, [2, 1, 0]]
            
            return rgb
            
        finally:
            os.unlink(local_path)
            
    def to_pil(self, rgb_array: np.ndarray) -> Image.Image:
        """Convert numpy RGB to PIL Image for VLM input."""
        return Image.fromarray(rgb_array, mode='RGB')
        
    def get_screen_dimensions(self) -> tuple[int, int]:
        """Return actual pixel dimensions for coordinate normalization."""
        return (self.width, self.height)
```

## VERIFIED TRANSPORT IMPLEMENTATION (MEmu 9 + fb0)

```python
# runtime/transport/memu_fb0.py
import subprocess
import numpy as np
from PIL import Image
import tempfile
import os

class MEmuFB0Transport:
    """
    VERIFIED transport for MEmu 9 Azur Lane.
    
    Confirmed working:
    - Device: 127.0.0.1:21513
    - fb0: 1152x864, 32bpp, stride 4608, driver hyperv_fb
    - Method: adb root  dd to /sdcard  adb pull (NOT exec-out cat, truncates)
    - adb root works; su does not exist on this image
    """
    
    def __init__(self,
                 host: str = "127.0.0.1",
                 port: int = 21513,
                 width: int = 1152,
                 height: int = 864,
                 bpp: int = 32):
        self.serial = f"{host}:{port}"
        self.width = width
        self.height = height
        self.stride = width * (bpp // 8)  # 4608
        self.frame_size = self.stride * height  # 3,981,312 bytes
        
    def ensure_root(self):
        """Enable adb root and wait for device to reconnect."""
        subprocess.run(["adb", "-s", self.serial, "root"], check=True)
        # CRITICAL: adbd restarts after root, must wait
        subprocess.run(["adb", "-s", self.serial, "wait-for-device"], check=True)
        
    def verify_focus(self) -> bool:
        """Check if Azur Lane is focused. Returns False if not."""
        # NOTE: No shell pipes in subprocess. Parse in Python.
        result = subprocess.run(
            ["adb", "-s", self.serial, "shell", "dumpsys", "window", "windows"],
            capture_output=True, text=True, check=True
        )
        # Parse output for mCurrentFocus
        for line in result.stdout.splitlines():
            if "mCurrentFocus" in line or "mFocusedApp" in line:
                return "com.YoStarEN.AzurLane" in line
        return False
        
    def capture(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """
        Capture frame from fb0.
        Returns: RGB numpy array (H, W, 3) uint8
        
        Raises:
            RuntimeError: if frame size mismatch or decode fails
        """
        # 1. Ensure root session
        self.ensure_root()
        
        # 2. Capture to device storage (reliable path)
        remote_path = "/sdcard/fb0_capture.raw"
        subprocess.run([
            "adb", "-s", self.serial, "shell",
            f"dd if=/dev/graphics/fb0 of={remote_path} bs={self.frame_size} count=1"
        ], check=True, capture_output=True)
        
        # 3. Pull to local temp file (verified reliable, exec-out cat truncates)
        with tempfile.NamedTemporaryFile(suffix=".raw", delete=False) as tmp:
            local_path = tmp.name
            
        try:
            subprocess.run([
                "adb", "-s", self.serial, "pull", remote_path, local_path
            ], check=True, capture_output=True)
            
            # 4. Read and validate size
            with open(local_path, "rb") as f:
                raw = f.read()
                
            if len(raw) != self.frame_size:
                raise RuntimeError(
                    f"Frame size mismatch: got {len(raw)}, expected {self.frame_size}"
                )
                
            # 5. Decode (CHANNEL ORDER TO BE VALIDATED - see below)
            # TODO: Validate BGRA vs RGBA against known screenshot
            # Current assumption: BGRA based on Android convention
            bgra = np.frombuffer(raw, dtype=np.uint8).reshape(self.height, self.width, 4)
            
            # Convert BGRA to RGB (drop alpha)
            rgb = bgra[:, :, [2, 1, 0]]
            
            return rgb
            
        finally:
            os.unlink(local_path)
            
    def to_pil(self, rgb_array: np.ndarray) -> Image.Image:
        """Convert numpy RGB to PIL Image for VLM input."""
        return Image.fromarray(rgb_array, mode='RGB')
        
    def get_screen_dimensions(self) -> tuple[int, int]:
        """Return actual pixel dimensions for coordinate normalization."""
        return (self.width, self.height)
```

## codex: review the number of mcp servers skills and tool i...

review the number of mcp servers skills and tool in antigravity: It looks like you've run into a known bug with **Google Antigravity** (the AI-powered IDE/agent environment) that has been hitting developers recently.

The error message `could not convert a single message before hitting truncation` means that the "Cortex" engine (the orchestration layer) is trying to pack so much information into the initial "handshake" with the AI model that it exceeds the token limit before your prompt is even sent. 

### Why this is happening
Even if you just type "Hello," the system attempts to load the metadata for every **Skill** and **MCP (Model Context Protocol) Server** you have enabled. If you have a large library of skills (some users reported issues once they hit 300+ skills), the list of tool definitions alone becomes too large for the context window to handle.

### How to Fix It

Depending on your setup, try these steps in order:

#### 1. Clear your Global Skills (Most Effective)
The most common "quick fix" is to clear out your local skills directory, which forces the agent to stop loading bloated metadata.
* **Windows:** Go to `C:\Users\<YourUsername>\.gemini\antigravity\skills`
* **macOS/Linux:** Look in `~/.gemini/antigravity/skills`
* **Action:** Back up these files to another folder and then **delete them** from the `skills` directory. Restart Antigravity and try a simple prompt.

#### 2. Disable MCP Servers
If you aren't using many skills but have several MCP servers active:
* Open the **Agent Panel** in Antigravity.
* Click the **three-dot menu (...)** > **MCP Servers** > **Manage MCP Servers**.
* Disable any servers you aren't actively using for your current task.

#### 3. Roll Back (If on v1.20.5)
If this started immediately after a recent update, you might need to revert to a stable build (like **1.19.6**) until a patch is released.
* **Windows (PowerShell):** `winget install --name "antigravity" --version 1.19.6 --force`
* **Note:** You should disable "Background Updates" in the Editor Settings immediately after rolling back to prevent it from auto-updating back to the buggy version.

#### 4. Use a Different Model
Some users have noted that this error is more prevalent when using **Gemini Flash** or **Pro** models due to how the `TrajectoryChatConverter` formats the messages for them. Switching to a **Claude** model (if available in your tier) can sometimes bypass the truncation logic as it uses a different conversion path.

### Summary for your Trajectory ID
Your specific Trajectory ID (`eee3f1ac...`) confirms that the crash occurred in the `CascadeManager` while trying to execute the "Helper" function. This is a "pre-flight" failure, meaning the AI never actually saw your message because the system crashed while preparing it.

**Would you like me to help you draft a bug report for the Google AI Developers forum with your specific stack trace?**

## codex: do you agree wit hthis diagnosis? It **did connect...

do you agree wit hthis diagnosis? It **did connect to MEmu**. The agents diagnosis got muddled because it conflated three different things. 🔧

## What actually worked

From the log:

* `doctor` saw:

  * `adb_reachable: true`
  * `serial: 127.0.0.1:21503`
  * `device_online: true`
* `connect` succeeded via **ADB fallback**
* `capture` succeeded repeatedly at **1280x720**
* `probe maa` passed all 7 checks
* `probe scrcpy` attached successfully
* full `probe session` passed after the gating fix

So the transport layer was **never fundamentally failing to reach MEmu**.

## Why it looked like it couldnt connect

There are really **3 separate issues**:

### 1. The health check defined connected too strictly

`doctor` treated the absence of `maamcp` / `maafw` as a failure, even though:

* ADB could reach the emulator
* the configured serial was correct
* the device was online
* the fallback controller path worked

That means the agent was using a **tool discovery failure** as if it were a **transport connectivity failure**.

That is the main reason the session looked broken.

### 2. The session probe gated on the wrong signal

The session probe had logic like:

* run `doctor`
* if `doctor != PASS`, abort before running deeper probes

But `doctor` was failing for native tool not installed, not cannot talk to emulator.

So the probe was effectively saying:

> I refuse to test the working fallback path because the preferred path isnt present.

That is a **bad gate design**. Once the agent relaxed that gate and allowed continuation when `device_online == true`, the session probe passed.

### 3. Blank screenshots were misread as a connection symptom

The captured PNGs were valid:

* full resolution
* valid dimensions
* fast capture timing

They were just mostly white / blank.

That points to things like:

* MEmu on a blank/loading/home screen
* protected/black/empty surface content
* game not launched / wrong window state
* emulator rendering state issue

That is **not** evidence that the agent failed to connect. It is evidence that the **observation target was visually empty**.

## Root cause, in one sentence

The agent confused **native MaaMCP stack not installed** with **cannot connect to MEmu,** and then let that false failure block the rest of the probe flow.

## Architecture mistake underneath it

The system appears to have two layers of truth:

* **Transport truth**: can I reach the emulator over ADB and interact with it?
* **Preferred substrate truth**: is the preferred MaaMCP/native stack installed?

Those should produce different verdicts.

Right now the agent effectively had:

* no `maamcp`  fail

What it should have had is something closer to:

* ADB reachable + device online + fallback control works  **transport pass**
* native Maa stack unavailable  **degraded / warning**
* scrcpy usable only for debug observation  **debug_only**

## What the correct interpretation should have been

A clean interpretation of the run would be:

* **MEmu connectivity:** pass
* **ADB transport:** pass
* **Control path:** pass via fallback
* **Capture path:** pass
* **Preferred native Maa stack:** unavailable
* **scrcpy runtime observation path:** not suitable on Windows, debug only

## Why the agent seemed confused

Because it was mixing **capability detection**, **health status**, and **runtime readiness** into one binary verdict. That leads to false negatives.

It should separate:

* **reachable**
* **operable**
* **preferred stack available**
* **fully production-ready**

Those are not the same thing.

## Practical conclusion

The problem was **not cant connect to MEmu.**
The real problem was:

> the probe/health logic was over-constrained and incorrectly classified a degraded-but-working setup as failure.

Thats why once the gating logic changed, everything lit up green.

## Best concise diagnosis

**MEmu was reachable the whole time.**
The failure was in the agents **health model**, not the emulator connection:

* it required `maamcp` for a PASS,
* it aborted session testing on that strict verdict,
* and it misinterpreted blank screenshots as transport trouble.

If you want, I can turn this into a tight postmortem with:

* symptom
* actual cause
* contributing causes
* code/design fixes
* recommended verdict taxonomy.

## codex: pushback or agree: hat's documented vs. implemente...

pushback or agree: hat's documented vs. implemented

Not implemented
The 10-candidate analysis is solid
MaaMCP + MaaFramework as primary, scrcpy as debug-only  that's well-reasoned and consistent with the live probe. The rejection of minicap/minitouch (stale), uiautomator2/Appium (XML-hierarchy-first, wrong for Unity games), and Maestro (YAML-flow-first, wrong model) is correct.

The 5-tier readiness model is over-engineered
health-heartbeat-logging.md:59-84 proposes:

unreachable
reachable
operable
preferred_stack_ready
production_ready
The last two are problematic in practice. "preferred_stack_ready" vs "operable" collapses at runtime  once maafw is installed and working, the system just is operable via preferred. The distinction only matters as a deployment gate, not a runtime tier. "production_ready" requires burn-in proof that can't come from a single probe run.

A cleaner 3-tier model is sufficient:

unreachable  no ADB
operable     ADB + capture + input work
down         capture or input broken
With explicit degradation flags: preferred_stack_missing, debug_only_visual, frame_freshness_unproven, action_ack_weak.

The scrcpy Windows verdict is correctly documented
debug_only is accurate based on the evidence  rom1v himself confirmed it in Feb 2024: "No" (for a Windows equivalent of V4L2). The doc should cite this directly rather than reasoning from the 2019 issue.

The gap that matters
The real problem: DoctorReport.verdict is computed as device_online and manifest.all_required_found  meaning no maamcp = FAIL, even with a working ADB fallback. This conflates tool discovery with transport health.

The fix in cmd_probe_session (soft gate when device_online=true) patched the symptom. The right fix is making verdict reflect what DoctorReport already tracks  it has separate adb_reachable, device_online, maamcp_available, scrcpy_available fields. Those should each be reported independently, not collapsed.

Recommendation
Don't write more docs. The substrate decision is made. What's actually needed is:

Implement the 3-tier readiness model (not 5-tier) in models.py + health.py
Expose per-layer status in DoctorReport.to_dict() so callers see adb_reachable, control_surface, observation_surface separately
Add degradation codes as a simple list[str] field
Remove the hard all_required_found gate from doctor verdict  maamcp missing should be a degradation flag, not a FAIL
The documentation is sufficient. The implementation is behind.

where are the docs?

---

## codex: review this: // ==UserScript==

review this: // ==UserScript==
// @name         Civitai Image Downloader and Metadata Extractor
// @name:zh-CN   Civitai 图像下载及元数据提取器
// @namespace    http://tampermonkey.net/
// @version      2.3
// @description  FINAL VERSION. Reliably works with Civitai's SPA navigation. No more refresh needed.
// @description:zh-CN 新增下载记录功能，防止重复下载。
// @author       Your Name (with major enhancements)
// @match        https://civitai.com/*
// @icon         https://civitai.com/favicon-32x32.png
// @grant        GM_download
// @grant        GM_log
// @grant        GM_setValue
// @grant        GM_getValue
// @grant        GM_addStyle
// @license      MIT
// @run-at       document-idle
// @downloadURL https://update.greasyfork.org/scripts/539298/Civitai%20Image%20Downloader%20and%20Metadata%20Extractor.user.js
// @updateURL https://update.greasyfork.org/scripts/539298/Civitai%20Image%20Downloader%20and%20Metadata%20Extractor.meta.js
// ==/UserScript==

(function() {
    'use strict';

    // --- 配置 & 常量 ---
    const AUTO_DOWNLOAD_KEY = 'civitaiDownloader_autoMode';
    const DOWNLOADED_IDS_KEY = 'civitaiDownloader_downloadedIds';

    // --- 添加自定义样式 ---
    GM_addStyle(`
        .civitai-downloader-toggle.active { background-color: #228be6 !important; border-color: #228be6 !important; }
        .civitai-downloader-toggle.downloaded { background-color: #2f9e44 !important; border-color: #2f9e44 !important; }
    `);

    // --- 全局状态变量，用于防止重复初始化 ---
    let lastProcessedUrl = '';

    // ==============================================================================
    // --- 主程序入口，现在由导航事件触发 ---
    // ==============================================================================
    function mainApp() {
        const currentUrl = window.location.href;

        // 检查URL是否是图片页，并且与上次处理的URL不同
        if (currentUrl.includes('/images/') && currentUrl !== lastProcessedUrl) {
            console.log(`Civitai Downloader: Image page detected - ${currentUrl}. Initializing...`);
            lastProcessedUrl = currentUrl; // 标记为正在处理

            // 使用轮询来等待按钮容器加载完毕
            const pollInterval = setInterval(() => {
                const buttonContainer = document.querySelector('svg.tabler-icon-download')?.closest('button')?.parentElement;
                // 确保容器存在且我们的按钮还未注入
                if (buttonContainer && !buttonContainer.querySelector('.civitai-downloader-toggle')) {
                    clearInterval(pollInterval);
                    runScriptOnPage(buttonContainer);
                }
            }, 500);

            // 15秒后停止轮询，以防页面结构变化导致死循环
            setTimeout(() => clearInterval(pollInterval), 15000);
        } else if (!currentUrl.includes('/images/')) {
            // 如果我们导航到了非图片页，重置URL标记，以便下次能重新进入
            lastProcessedUrl = '';
        }
    }

    // ==============================================================================
    // --- 脚本核心逻辑 ---
    // ==============================================================================
    function runScriptOnPage(buttonContainer) {
        const imageId = window.location.pathname.split('/')[2];
        if (!imageId) return;

        const downloadButton = buttonContainer.querySelector('svg.tabler-icon-download')?.closest('button');
        if(!downloadButton) return;

        let isAutoMode = GM_getValue(AUTO_DOWNLOAD_KEY, true);
        const downloadedIds = GM_getValue(DOWNLOADED_IDS_KEY, {});
        const hasBeenDownloaded = !!downloadedIds[imageId];

        const toggleButton = createToggleButton(downloadButton);
        buttonContainer.insertBefore(toggleButton, downloadButton);

        function updateToggleVisual() {
            toggleButton.classList.remove('active', 'downloaded');
            if (hasBeenDownloaded) {
                toggleButton.classList.add('downloaded');
                toggleButton.title = "此页已下载过 (点击原下载按钮可强制重新下载)";
            } else if (isAutoMode) {
                toggleButton.classList.add('active');
                toggleButton.title = "自动下载模式已开启";
            } else {
                toggleButton.title = "自动下载模式已关闭 (点击原下载按钮手动触发)";
            }
        }
        updateToggleVisual();

        toggleButton.addEventListener('click', () => {
            isAutoMode = !isAutoMode;
            GM_setValue(AUTO_DOWNLOAD_KEY, isAutoMode);
            updateToggleVisual();
        });

        downloadButton.addEventListener('click', (event) => {
            event.preventDefault();
            event.stopPropagation();
            startFullDownload(imageId);
        }, true);

        if (isAutoMode && !hasBeenDownloaded) {
            startFullDownload(imageId);
        }
    }


    // ==============================================================================
    // --- 导航事件监听 (最终解决方案) ---
    // ==============================================================================
    // 1. 劫持 history.pushState
    const originalPushState = history.pushState;
    history.pushState = function(...args) {
        // 先执行原始的 pushState
        const result = originalPushState.apply(this, args);
        // 然后触发一个自定义事件，并延迟执行我们的主程序
        window.dispatchEvent(new Event('pushstate'));
        setTimeout(mainApp, 500); // 延迟执行以等待DOM更新
        return result;
    };

    // 2. 监听 history.popstate (浏览器前进/后退按钮)
    window.addEventListener('popstate', () => {
        setTimeout(mainApp, 500);
    });

    // 3. 首次加载页面时，也手动运行一次
    setTimeout(mainApp, 1500); // 首次加载延迟稍长，确保所有内容渲染完毕


    // --- 核心下载逻辑和其他辅助函数 (保持不变) ---
    async function startFullDownload(imageId) {console.log("Civitai Downloader: Starting full download process...");try {const metadata = extractAllMetadata();if (!metadata) return;const textContent = formatMetadataAsText(metadata);const txtFilename = `${imageId}.txt`;downloadTextFile(textContent, txtFilename);await downloadImageWhenReady(imageId);markAsDownloaded(imageId);} catch (error) {console.error("Civitai Downloader: An error occurred in the main download function.", error);}}
    function markAsDownloaded(imageId) {const downloadedIds = GM_getValue(DOWNLOADED_IDS_KEY, {});downloadedIds[imageId] = true;GM_setValue(DOWNLOADED_IDS_KEY, downloadedIds);const toggleButton = document.querySelector('.civitai-downloader-toggle');if (toggleButton) {toggleButton.classList.remove('active');toggleButton.classList.add('downloaded');toggleButton.title = "此页已下载过 (点击原下载按钮可强制重新下载)";}}
    function createToggleButton(referenceButton) {const toggleButton = referenceButton.cloneNode(true);toggleButton.classList.add('civitai-downloader-toggle');const svg = toggleButton.querySelector('svg');svg.innerHTML = `<path d="M20 11a8.1 8.1 0 0 0 -15.5 -2m-.5 -4v4h4"></path><path d="M4 13a8.1 8.1 0 0 0 15.5 2m.5 4v-4h-4"></path>`;svg.classList.remove('tabler-icon-download');svg.classList.add('tabler-icon-refresh');return toggleButton;}
    function extractAllMetadata() {const metadata = {};metadata.sourceUrl = window.location.href;const prompts = extractPrompts();metadata.positivePrompt = prompts.positive;metadata.negativePrompt = prompts.negative;metadata.resources = extractResources();metadata.details = extractDetails();return metadata;}
    function extractPrompts() {const prompts = { positive: "Not found", negative: "Not found" };let generationDataContainer = null;const allHeaders = document.querySelectorAll('h3.mantine-Title-root');for (const h of allHeaders) {if (h.textContent.trim().toLowerCase() === 'generation data') {generationDataContainer = h.parentElement;break;}}if (!generationDataContainer) {generationDataContainer = document;}const promptElements = generationDataContainer.querySelectorAll('.mantine-1c2skr8');if (promptElements.length > 0) prompts.positive = promptElements[0].textContent.trim();if (promptElements.length > 1) prompts.negative = promptElements[1].textContent.trim();return prompts;}
    function extractResources() {const resources = [];let resourceList = null;const allHeaders = document.querySelectorAll('h3.mantine-Title-root');for (const h of allHeaders) {if (h.textContent.trim().toLowerCase() === 'resources') {const container = h.parentElement;if (container && container.nextElementSibling && container.nextElementSibling.tagName === 'UL') {resourceList = container.nextElementSibling;break;}}}if (!resourceList) {resourceList = document.querySelector('ul.flex.list-none.flex-col');}if (!resourceList) return ["Resource list not found."];resourceList.querySelectorAll('li').forEach(item => {const linkElement = item.querySelector('a[href*="/models/"]');const nameElement = item.querySelector('div.mantine-12h10m4');const versionElement = item.querySelector('div.mantine-nvo449');const typeElement = item.querySelector('div.mantine-qcxgtg span.mantine-Badge-inner');const resource = {};if (nameElement) resource.name = nameElement.textContent.trim();if (linkElement) resource.link = `https://civitai.com${linkElement.getAttribute('href')}`;if (versionElement) resource.version = versionElement.textContent.trim();if (typeElement) resource.type = typeElement.textContent.trim();const weightElement = item.querySelector('div.mantine-j55fvo span.mantine-Badge-inner');if (weightElement) resource.weight = weightElement.textContent.trim();resources.push(resource);});return resources;}
    function extractDetails() {const details = {};const detailsContainer = document.querySelector('div.flex.flex-wrap.gap-2');if (!detailsContainer) return details;const detailBadges = detailsContainer.querySelectorAll(':scope > div.mantine-Badge-root');detailBadges.forEach(badge => {const text = badge.textContent.trim();const parts = text.split(/:(.*)/s);if (parts.length >= 2) {const key = parts[0].trim();const value = parts[1].trim();details[key] = value;}});return details;}
    function formatMetadataAsText(metadata) {let content = "Positive Prompt:\n" + metadata.positivePrompt + "\n\n";content += "Negative Prompt:\n" + metadata.negativePrompt + "\n\n";content += "--- Details ---\n";for (const [key, value] of Object.entries(metadata.details)) {content += `${key}: ${value}\n`;}content += "\n--- Resources ---\n";if (metadata.resources.length > 0 && typeof metadata.resources[0] === 'string') {content += metadata.resources[0] + "\n\n";} else {metadata.resources.forEach(res => {content += `Type: ${res.type || 'N/A'}\n`;content += `Name: ${res.name || 'N/A'}\n`;content += `Version: ${res.version || 'N/A'}\n`;if (res.weight) content += `Weight: ${res.weight}\n`;content += `Link: ${res.link || 'N/A'}\n\n`;});}content += "--- Source ---\n";content += `Image URL: ${metadata.sourceUrl}\n`;return content;}
    function downloadTextFile(textContent, filename) {const blob = new Blob([textContent], { type: 'text/plain;charset=utf-8' });const dataUrl = URL.createObjectURL(blob);GM_download({url: dataUrl,name: filename,onload: () => {URL.revokeObjectURL(dataUrl);},onerror: (err) => {URL.revokeObjectURL(dataUrl);}});}
    async function downloadImageWhenReady(imageId) {return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {const pollingInterval = 250;const maxWaitTime = 10000;let totalWait = 0;const imageElement = document.querySelector('img.EdgeImage_image__iH4_q');if (!imageElement) {return reject("Image element not found.");}const poller = setInterval(() => {const currentSrc = imageElement.src;if (currentSrc && currentSrc.startsWith('http') && currentSrc.includes('original=true')) {clearInterval(poller);downloadImage(currentSrc, imageId).then(resolve).catch(reject);} else {totalWait += pollingInterval;if (totalWait >= maxWaitTime) {clearInterval(poller);reject("Timed out");}}}, pollingInterval);});}
    function downloadImage(imageUrl, imageId) {return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {try {const urlPath = new URL(imageUrl).pathname;const extension = urlPath.substring(urlPath.lastIndexOf('.'));const newImageFilename = `${imageId}${extension}`;GM_download({url: imageUrl,name: newImageFilename,onload: () => {resolve();},onerror: (err) => {reject(err);}});} catch (e) {reject(e);}});}
})();

## codex: So, what the fuck? Like, why did we even bother do...

So, what the fuck? Like, why did we even bother doing this again? And then what is agent path, and did we fight the tooling or did we leverage the tooling?
You're right to call this out. Let me be direct.

What we built and why
The MaaAdapter is a Maa-shaped adapter with an ADB fallback. The intent was correct  wrap the preferred tool (Maa) and have a fallback when it's unavailable. That follows the architecture doc.

But the current state is: the fallback IS the entire thing. We're not using Maa, we're using raw ADB shell primitives through a Maa-shaped hole.

What agent_path is
It's the filesystem path to the MaaAgent.so binary that must be deployed on the Android device itself. MaaFramework's Python bindings (AdbController) talk to that agent over ADB. Without it, MaaFramework can't initialize.

The chain is:

Python (adapter)  maa.controller.AdbController  ADB  MaaAgent.so (on Android device)
No agent on the device = no MaaFramework = you get adb_direct.

Did we fight or leverage?
We fought the tooling by building a wrapper we never completed, and leveraged the tooling by using ADB primitives that always work.

The honest summary:

What we said
What we actually did
"MaaFramework is the primary substrate"
ADB shell primitives  MaaFramework never initialized
"MaaMCP is the agent-facing surface"
agent_path: null  MCP server not started
"borrowed control tool ownership"
We borrowed nothing. We just used ADB directly.
The substrate selection plan said Maa was the winner. The code says Maa is the winner. The config says null. These three things do not agree.

What to do
Either:

Commit to ADB-direct as the blessed substrate and rename maamcp.py  adb_primitives.py. Remove the MaaFramework wrapper entirely until agent_path is real. This matches what you're actually running.
Actually install MaaMCP/MaaFramework and populate agent_path. This requires the MCP server running and the .so on the Android device.
